          <div class="article article-large cleared" data-original-title="City going back to office in EIGHT days as stay at home rule dropped" itemprop="itemListElement" itemscope="" itemtype="//schema.org/ListItem">
           <meta content="1" itemprop="position"/>
           <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
            <a href="/money/markets/article-9383741/City-going-office-EIGHT-days-stay-home-rule-dropped.html" itemprop="url">
             City goes back to the office in EIGHT days: US banks in first wave of firms returning as stay at home rule dropped
            </a>
           </h2>
           <a href="/money/markets/article-9383741/City-going-office-EIGHT-days-stay-home-rule-dropped.html">
            <img alt="City going back to office in EIGHT days as stay at home rule dropped" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/20/13/40715692-0-image-m-124_1616246894237.jpg" height="185" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="308"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="City going back to office in EIGHT days as stay at home rule dropped" height="185" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/20/13/40715692-0-image-m-124_1616246894237.jpg" width="308"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <div class="articletext-holder">
            <p>
             Goldman Sachs, JP Morgan and Credit Suisse are among those paving the way for workers to begin to return. It is understood that bankers have had concerns about whether they could be penalised by the Government for bringing more staff back to the office so soon. Only some key traders and staff who have not been able to work from home have been allowed in up until now.One banker said the Government gave a nod and a wink that they will not be punished for allowing staff to return. The Governments stay at home rule will end on March 29.Official advice calls for people to continue to work from home where they can.
            </p>

If the courts side with RGL, it could result in HargreavesLansdown being required to pay compensation totalling hundreds of millions of pounds. RGL has also launched a simultaneous legal action against Link,the fund's authorised corporate director, whose role was to protect the investors' interests.

            <a href="/money/bills/article-9383705/New-energy-rating-white-goods-help-cut-bills.html" itemprop="url">
             New ratings system for large electrical goods could result in household bills being cut by as much as 100 a year
            </a>
           </h2>
           <div class="articletext">
            <a href="/money/bills/article-9383705/New-energy-rating-white-goods-help-cut-bills.html">
             <img alt="" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/20/14/40717556-0-image-m-79_1616251735100.jpg" height="115" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="154"/>
             <noscript>
              <img alt="" height="115" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/20/14/40717556-0-image-m-79_1616251735100.jpg" width="154"/>
             </noscript>
            </a>
            <p>
             It is part of a shake-up of the efficiency grading system by the Government for new products such as fridges, washing machines and TVs.
            </p>
           </div>

          var l_twitterLinkChannel, l_facebookLinkChannel, l_twitterVia, l_facebookText;
if(document.domain.indexOf("/") !== -1 || document.location.pathname.indexOf("/money") !== -1) {
  l_twitterLinkChannel =  'ThisIsMoney';
  l_facebookLinkChannel =  '/pages/This-is-Money/310555847252';

  l_facebookText = 'This is Money';
} else {
  l_twitterLinkChannel =  currentChannelTwitterFollow || 'MailOnline';

  l_facebookText = 'MailOnline';

function goToFB(){
  DM.later("bundle", function (){
    DM.pageEvents.fireEvent(DM.pageEvents.SOCIAL_SHARE_CLICKED, {
      pageMetadata: DM.getPageMetadata({articleId: 'non-article'}),
      site: "facebook",
      placement: "non-native"
    });
    window.open("https://www.facebook.com/" + l_facebookLinkChannel);
  });
}
function followOnTwitter() {
  DM.later("bundle", function (){
    DM.pageEvents.fireEvent(DM.pageEvents.SOCIAL_SHARE_CLICKED, {
      pageMetadata: DM.getPageMetadata({articleId: 'non-article'}),
      site: "twitter",
      placement: "non-native"
    });
    var width = 575,
    height = 400,
    left = (window.outerWidth - width) / 2,
    top = (window.outerHeight - height) / 2,
    url = this.href,
    opts = 'resizable=1,scrollbars=1,status=1' +
    ',width=' + width +
    ',height=' + height +
    ',top=' + top +
    ',left=' + left;
    var newwindow = window.open("https://twitter.com/intent/user?screen_name=" + l_twitterLinkChannel + "&related=" + l_twitterVia, "", opts);
  });
  return false;
}
DM.later("bundle", function (){
  Array.from(document.querySelectorAll('.twpuffbutton p')).forEach(function(elem) {
    elem.innerHTML = '<b>Follow</b><br>@' + l_twitterLinkChannel;
  });
  Array.from(document.querySelectorAll('.fbpuffbutton p')).forEach(function(elem) {
    elem.innerHTML = '<b>Follow</b><br>' + l_facebookText;
  });
});

          <div class="article article-large cleared" data-original-title="MIDAS SHARE TIPS:  BBGI could help with infrastructure projects" itemprop="itemListElement" itemscope="" itemtype="//schema.org/ListItem">
           <meta content="9" itemprop="position"/>
           <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
            <a href="/money/investing/article-9383731/MIDAS-SHARE-TIPS-BBGI-help-infrastructure-projects.html" itemprop="url">
             MIDAS SHARE TIPS: Governments are pledging to spend on infrastructure - they could do with help from the private sector, companies such as BBGI
            </a>
           </h2>
           <a href="/money/investing/article-9383731/MIDAS-SHARE-TIPS-BBGI-help-infrastructure-projects.html">
            <img alt="MIDAS SHARE TIPS:  BBGI could help with infrastructure projects" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/20/13/40715630-0-image-m-92_1616246476635.jpg" height="185" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="308"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="MIDAS SHARE TIPS:  BBGI could help with infrastructure projects" height="185" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/20/13/40715630-0-image-m-92_1616246476635.jpg" width="308"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <div class="articletext-holder">
            <p>
             BBGI specialises in essential assets such asroads, schools, hospitals, fire and police stations. The stock is 1.66 and should enjoy steady gains over the coming years, alongside generous dividends. BBGI's motto is: boring is beautiful. But boring can also yield rewards. The company has delivered consistent dividend and share price growth since flotation and aims to continue doing so. For investors in search of low-risk shares in an uncertain world, BBGI is a long-term buy.
            </p>

        <div class="article article-tri-headline" itemprop="itemListElement" itemscope="" itemtype="//schema.org/ListItem">
         <meta content="15" itemprop="position"/>
         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/podcast/article-9381475/How-save-invest-Isa-worth-doing-TiM-podcast.html" itemprop="url">
           How to save or invest in an Isa - and why it's still worth doing: This is Money podcast
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/podcast/article-9381475/How-save-invest-Isa-worth-doing-TiM-podcast.html">
           <img alt="How to save or invest in an Isa and why it's worth doing: TiM podcast" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/19/16/40687558-0-image-a-4_1616172328838.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="How to save or invest in an Isa and why it's worth doing: TiM podcast" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/19/16/40687558-0-image-a-4_1616172328838.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            What's the point in an Isa? This is a regular grumble as savings rates are now so low that earning 1 per cent would be a big deal. But wouldn't you rather have all of a small amount instead of a small amount minus tax? And if you are investing, an Isa makes a lot of sense - embracing your gains and dividends in a nice tax-free wrapper. On this week's podcast, Georgie Frost, Lee Boyce and Simon Lambert talk Isas: from the classics, cash and stocks and shares, to the upstarts the lifetime and junior strands.
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>

         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/experts/article-9371413/I-paid-7k-TV-firm-went-bust-rights.html" itemprop="url">
           GRACE ON THE CASE: I paid 7k for a Bang &amp; Olufsen TV and installation but the seller collapsed leaving me out of pocket
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/experts/article-9371413/I-paid-7k-TV-firm-went-bust-rights.html">
           <img alt="I paid 7k for a TV but firm went bust: What are my rights?" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/17/12/40584288-0-image-a-12_1615982600477.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>

           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            I bought a new Bang &amp; Olufsen television in early 2020, costing 7,375 in total when included with extras such as a wall bracket and sound system. Later in 2020, I contacted Bang &amp; Olufsen at Harrods to say it should wait until the lockdown had eased before delivering and installing. I was shocked to be informed the company which had operated Bang &amp; Olufsen at Harrods had gone into liquidation. The liquidator confirmed the company no longer operated and he could see little or no hope to recover the money I had paid for the TV. How can I get my TV or a refund?

         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/saving/article-9369607/Cash-Isas-worth-having.html" itemprop="url">
           Why you shouldn't simply turn your back on cash Isas:Rates are rock bottom and inflation will cost you but we all need a savings safety net
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/saving/article-9369607/Cash-Isas-worth-having.html">
           <img alt="Cash Isas: Are they still worth having?" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/16/22/40558994-0-image-a-6_1615932139388.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Cash Isas: Are they still worth having?" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/16/22/40558994-0-image-a-6_1615932139388.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            While savings rates may have fallen to pitiful lows, it would be unwise to abandon cash altogether. Each year, savers plough millions of pounds into tax-free cash Isas. But the once-popular accounts have lost their sparkle. Despite savers squirrelling away an extra 143.5bn over lockdown, the amount paid into cash Isas halved in January, compared with the previous year.
           </p>

        <div class="article article-tri-headline" itemprop="itemListElement" itemscope="" itemtype="//schema.org/ListItem">
         <meta content="34" itemprop="position"/>
         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/cardsloans/article-9372325/Visa-join-Mastercard-hiking-interchange-fees-UK-shoppers.html" itemprop="url">
           Regulators should crack down on 'profiteering' from card companies as Visa hikes interchange fees for shoppers buying from the EU by 475%
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/cardsloans/article-9372325/Visa-join-Mastercard-hiking-interchange-fees-UK-shoppers.html">
           <img alt="Visa to join Mastercard in hiking interchange fees for UK shoppers" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/17/14/40589640-0-image-a-21_1615992062690.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Visa to join Mastercard in hiking interchange fees for UK shoppers" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/17/14/40589640-0-image-a-21_1615992062690.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            Regulators have been urged to crack down on 'profiteering' by Britain's two largest card providers after Visa appeared to be joining Mastercard in massively hiking interchange fees after Brexit. Purchases made from European shops by UK shoppers will be subject to a fivefold increase in fees if they pay by credit card and a 475% rise if they pay by debit card. These fees are charged to retailers by their banks every time a card purchase is made to cover the cost of the transaction and are passed on to the bank which issues a shopper's card.
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="article-icon-links-container" data-followbutton="ThisIsMoney">

             Insurers paid out 202m to support families who lost loved ones due to coronavirus in 2020 including a 250k payout made the day after a death
            </a>
           </h2>
           <div class="articletext">
            <a href="/money/bills/article-9372565/Insurers-paid-202m-support-families-lost-loved-ones-Covid-2020.html">
             <img alt="" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/17/15/40593582-0-image-m-19_1615995714853.jpg" height="115" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="154"/>

             </noscript>
            </a>
            <p>
             Insurers paid out 202million - the equivalent of 553,000 every day - to support the families of people who sadly died due to Covid-19 in 2020, new data has revealed.

         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/investing/article-9369579/How-make-Isa-holdings-ethical.html" itemprop="url">
           'I want my money to make a difference': Is it possible to get ethical funds into an Isa and how do you do it?
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/investing/article-9369579/How-make-Isa-holdings-ethical.html">
           <img alt="How can I make my Isa holdings more ethical?" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/16/22/40560888-0-image-a-9_1615934287443.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="How can I make my Isa holdings more ethical?" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/16/22/40560888-0-image-a-9_1615934287443.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            Having investments need not trouble your conscience. There has been a surge in so-called responsible funds that promise to ensure that your money is put to good use. You can get a decent return on your savings and use them to back firms with a good record on issues such as climate change; or righteous causes, rather than the oil and tobacco industries.
           </p>

         <meta content="40" itemprop="position"/>
         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/pensions/article-9372131/Will-retire-2-6m-50s-track-work-indefinitely.html" itemprop="url">
           Will we ever retire? 2.6m people over 50 think they will now have to continue working 'indefinitely' as a result of the pandemic
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/pensions/article-9372131/Will-retire-2-6m-50s-track-work-indefinitely.html">
           <img alt="Will we ever retire? 2.6m over 50s on track to work 'indefinitely'" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/17/14/40589210-0-image-a-76_1615990919553.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Will we ever retire? 2.6m over 50s on track to work 'indefinitely'" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/17/14/40589210-0-image-a-76_1615990919553.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            Around 2.6million people over 50 in Britain expect to have to keep working 'indefinitely' as a result of the pandemic's impact on their finances, new findings claim. With the Covid-19 outbreak hitting many workers hard, new research by Legal and General suggests there are 429,000 unemployed over 50s in Britain, comprising one in four of all unemployed people. L&amp;G's latest research suggests that 1.45million people over 50 now plan to delay their retirement by about three years.
           </p>

          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/experts/article-9368121/ASK-TONY-did-home-insurer-slam-brakes-900-e-bike-claim.html">
           <img alt="ASK TONY: Why did home insurer slam brakes on 900 e-bike claim?" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/16/23/40563146-0-image-a-7_1615939022865.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>

            <img alt="ASK TONY: Why did home insurer slam brakes on 900 e-bike claim?" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/16/23/40563146-0-image-a-7_1615939022865.jpg" width="636"/>

          <div>
           <p>
            Two weeks ago our garage was broken into. They stole my mountain bike, worth 800, and my wife's e-bike. This was worth 1,500, but she bought it as an ex-display for 900. We informed our insurance company, RSA, and were told we could make a claim on my bike but not on my wife's e-bike because it is motorised and, therefore, not covered.
           </p>
          </div>

        <div class="article article-tri-headline" itemprop="itemListElement" itemscope="" itemtype="//schema.org/ListItem">
         <meta content="49" itemprop="position"/>
         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/diyinvesting/article-9368761/How-young-savers-25-bonus-1-000-Lifetime-Isa.html" itemprop="url">
           How young savers can get a 25% bonus of up to 1,000 with the Lifetime Isa... but beware an expensive penalty if you don't play by the rules
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/diyinvesting/article-9368761/How-young-savers-25-bonus-1-000-Lifetime-Isa.html">
           <img alt="How young savers can get a 25% bonus of up to 1,000 with the Lifetime Isa" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/16/17/40549238-0-image-a-10_1615914952229.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="How young savers can get a 25% bonus of up to 1,000 with the Lifetime Isa" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/16/17/40549238-0-image-a-10_1615914952229.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            Savers can deposit up to 4,000 every tax year into a Lifetime Isa. But the real advantage is the 25 per cent bonus on offer from the Government to top up your contributions. It means that for every 4 you save, the Government chips in 1. If you save the annual maximum of 4,000, you receive a 1,000 bonus. To qualify for a Lifetime Isa - often referred to as a Lisa - you must be aged between 18 and 39.
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="article-icon-links-container" data-followbutton="ThisIsMoney">

          <h6>
          </h6>

        <div class="article article-tri-headline" itemprop="itemListElement" itemscope="" itemtype="//schema.org/ListItem">
         <meta content="63" itemprop="position"/>
         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/markets/article-9381803/UK-borrows-19bn-coronavirus-battle.html" itemprop="url">
           Chancellor looks set to borrow less than feared this year - but deficit remains on course to be biggest since World War II
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/markets/article-9381803/UK-borrows-19bn-coronavirus-battle.html">
           <img alt="UK borrows another 19bn in coronavirus battle" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/19/20/40694458-0-image-a-96_1616184539196.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="UK borrows another 19bn in coronavirus battle" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/19/20/40694458-0-image-a-96_1616184539196.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            The Government borrowed a record 19.1billion last month as the cost of Covid continued to mount. It took borrowing for the first 11 months of the financial year to 278.8billion and drove the national debt to 2.13trillion. The Office for Budget Responsibility said that the full-year deficit was now likely to be lower than the 355billion it forecast just two weeks ago. However, it will still be the largest as a proportion of national income since the war.
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>

         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/experts/article-9354735/Do-share-bank-statements-KeySafe-new-flat.html" itemprop="url">
           I've been asked to log in to my online banking and share a year's worth of statements with a reference agency after renting a new flat. Is this right?
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/experts/article-9354735/Do-share-bank-statements-KeySafe-new-flat.html">
           <img alt="Do I have to share my bank statements with KeySafe for new flat?" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/12/10/40380126-0-image-a-12_1615546563342.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Do I have to share my bank statements with KeySafe for new flat?" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/12/10/40380126-0-image-a-12_1615546563342.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            The other weekend I moved into a new apartment. The estate agents said they use a third-party reference service which I thought nothing of. I received an email from this service, a company called KeySafe TV, and proceeded with the application. It seemed pretty normal up until the point of entering my bank details for the credit check, I clicked next and then it redirected me to my Barclays online banking service log in page. This seemed strange and wrong to me. I didn't log into my online banking as I didn't want anyone to have access. What is going on? Is this allowed?

          </a>

         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/cars/article-9355949/Jaguar-reveals-60th-birthday-E-Types-celebrating-Norman-Dewis.html" itemprop="url">
           Happy 60th birthday to the E-Type: Jaguar reveals revived cars celebrating the race overnight to its Geneva launch - as a coupe and convertible pair for 650k
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/cars/article-9355949/Jaguar-reveals-60th-birthday-E-Types-celebrating-Norman-Dewis.html">
           <img alt="Jaguar reveals 60th birthday E-Types celebrating Norman Dewis" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/12/16/40391612-0-image-a-41_1615567840408.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>

          <div>
           <p>
            The 60th birthday of the iconic Jaguar E-Type today is being celebrated with the creation of stunningly-restored Series 1 cars. The six sets of a coup and convertible E-Type are based on the two cars used for its famous public debut at the 1961 Geneva Motor Show. Costing around 650,000 for each pair, they honour the cars driven 'flat out' overnight from Coventry to the Swiss motor show - by legendary test-driver Norman Dewis and Jaguar PR Bob Berry - to arrive in time for the first press drives on March 15.

         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/diyinvesting/article-9363631/Dividend-Hero-investment-trusts-2021-revealed-Payouts-rose-market-collapsed.html" itemprop="url">
           The Dividend Hero investment trusts that raised payouts even as firms cut... and some have lifted income since The Graduate hit the big screen in 1967
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/diyinvesting/article-9363631/Dividend-Hero-investment-trusts-2021-revealed-Payouts-rose-market-collapsed.html">
           <img alt="Dividend Heroes 2021: Trusts that raised payouts as firms hacked back" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/15/12/40491984-0-image-a-4_1615812602273.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Dividend Heroes 2021: Trusts that raised payouts as firms hacked back" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/15/12/40491984-0-image-a-4_1615812602273.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            The 19-strong Dividend Hero list features trusts that lifted their payments to investors, despite a 41 per cent collapse in UK dividends as companies slashed costs in the face of the coronavirus crisis. A trio continued their impressive history that dates back 54 years. City of London, Bankers and Alliance Trust have raised dividend payments every year since 1967, when the Beatles reached number one with All You Need is Love and Dustin Hoffman starred in The Graduate.
           </p>

         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/bills/article-9358259/Are-dangers-e-scooters-high-price-pay.html" itemprop="url">
           E-scooters will save you money on your commute, but they still aren't legal: Are the dangers too high a price to pay?
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/bills/article-9358259/Are-dangers-e-scooters-high-price-pay.html">
           <img alt="Are the dangers of e-scooters too high a price to pay?" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/13/13/40418650-0-image-a-10_1615641458769.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Are the dangers of e-scooters too high a price to pay?" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/13/13/40418650-0-image-a-10_1615641458769.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            What most people do not know is that it is illegal to ride an e-scooter on a road, pavement, bus lane or even bike lane. Pretty much anywhere in fact, unless you are trundling along in a designated 'trial' area and using an officially rented scooter. But all this could change later this year when pilot schemes across Britain come to an end and a huge swarm of 'legal' e-scooters could start to spread across our land. Illegal riders like me rarely face penalties - traffic wardens and the police are not usually interested. As Toby Walne discovered, an e-scooter is a licence to menace others.
           </p>

         <h2 class="linkro-darkred">
          <a href="/money/investing/article-9360551/Heres-build-ISA-tax-haven.html" itemprop="url">
           There's a valuable financial refuge Rishi hasn't raided: JEFF PRESTRIDGE'S tips on how to build your own Isa tax haven
          </a>
         </h2>
         <div class="articletext">
          <a href="/money/investing/article-9360551/Heres-build-ISA-tax-haven.html">
           <img alt="Here's how to build your very own Isa tax haven" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/14/13/40451780-0-image-a-38_1615730236557.jpg" height="382" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" style="max-width:100%" width="636"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Here's how to build your very own Isa tax haven" height="382" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/03/14/13/40451780-0-image-a-38_1615730236557.jpg" width="636"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <div>
           <p>
            In this brilliant report, we explain how you can use the simplicity and tax-freedom of Isas to help build your long-term wealth and start putting in place your retirement finances (however young you now may be). Look upon Isas as wealth building blocks that can be employed at any age - even children can get a slice of the Isa action - and while their main purpose is wealth creation they can also be used to help build a deposit for a first home.
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
